Finished this, here's the breakdown:   I did this for 22 days in a row, I supplemented my normal workout (back/chest/leg/ab days). I did not modify my diet (chicken/salmon with rice and healthy food about 60% of meals, salads 20% of meals, 20% less healthy food. During this time I went to the gym 7 days a week, not skipping a day. 1st exercise: I liked this one, but I struggled to keep my legs completely straight. 2nd exercise: I either didn't do the step through plank correctly, or it was too easy. (I found myself not getting an ab workout but a plank work out and my arms would get tired.)  3rd exercise: X-men crunches are my favorite 4th exercise: I modified this to do 5 on each side before alternating. I felt more of the mind-muscle connection, and it extended how long I could do it before my arms gave up. 5th: Jack knives were the hardest, and I could never get 1 full cycle. Good workout but my lower back would start to hurt really quickly. 6th: Liked this one, felt a bit of a burn.  Overall, I saw a little bit of change, especially when I did this workout after an ab day. After I finished 22 days, I went back to 6 days a week of working out and have been doing this every workout since. I definitely feel improvement and my abs are stronger, but the visual results are slightly disappointing.   *on a side note: my other compound exercises, squats, bench press, deadlifts, etc. have all improved significantly, so overall I'm pleased with the results of training abs while still getting stronger.

Thread the needle doesn't seem to work for me. Puts stress on my shoulders (rear delts), feet and back, but I don't notice any kind of ab work, not even after 4 sets. I try to get them involved as much as I can, but they don't seem to care.  I think I have a problem with planks in general, whether it's twisting pistons, tuck planks, pendulum planks, etc. my abs don't seem to care much, my shoulders, triceps, upper back and waist end up making most of the work (even when I try to remove those from the equation, my abs do little work).  I mean, the conclusion I should apparently draw from this is that I have weak abs, but truth is they aren't.  They are quite resilient, actually, so much so that I need to put weights on my ankles in order to challenge them when I do ab training.   For instance, I've been doing your 6 pack promise sore in 6 ab routine for 9 months now...(well, it's actually a sore in 12 version, since 6 minutes alone don't cut it for me). I started doing that routine without weights and at first it was challenging enough for my abs to get sore. But as time passed I noticed that my abs weren't being challenged anymore, so I started training with weighted ankle bands, it worked. Those figure 8s, windshield wipers, starfish crunches, etc. became harder to perform, and my abs were grateful (well, I was grateful, my abs were actually dying ,^^).   Now I'm training with 2kg ankle bands on each leg and I'll probably increase the weight to 3kg in the near future. Are my abs still too weak for planks? What's going on? Why is my back always trying to take all the credit?

I'm 16% bf can I follow abs workout?
Okay guys, I've been reading some of the comments on here and everybody's asking did you get a 6 pack from it. It depends on the person. If someone has very low fat content, it's more than likely you will or can after a few rounds of this. If you're a bit too big to have visible abs buts still very fit and toned everywhere else, it's either your body or your diet. You can work abs all day but if you don't have a decent diet, a little determination and some time you won't get them.   To summarize, working your abs does NOT burn the fat over them unless that's all you have which is unlikely due to how the human body works. A diet and routine exercise is what will do it for you. It takes but 15-30 minutes a day to do this, at least for me so there shouldn't be any excuse not to at least try it but don't get pissed if you don't have abs at the 22 day mark.
